id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> (64.6)</li><li><a href="#cite_note-census2010-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Brazilians</b> (<i>brasileiros</i> in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[bɾaziˈlejɾus]</a></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> are citizens of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. A Brazilian can also be a person born abroad to a Brazilian parent or <a href="/wiki/Legal_guardian" title="Legal guardian">legal guardian</a> as well as a persons who acquired <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_nationality_law" title="Brazilian nationality law">Brazilian citizenship</a>. Brazil is a <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic society">multiethnic society</a>, which means that it is home to people of many different ethnic origins. As a result, majority of Brazilians do not equate their <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationality</a> with their ethnicity, usually embracing and espousing both simultaneously.
</p><p>In the period after the colonization of the Brazilian territory by <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, during much of the XVI century, the word "Brazilian" was given to the Portuguese merchants of <a href="/wiki/Brazilwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilwood">Brazilwood</a>, designating exclusively the name of such profession, since the inhabitants of the land were, in most of them, <a href="/wiki/Native_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Brazilian">indigenous</a> or Portuguese born in Portugal, or in the territory now called Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, long before the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a>, in 1822, both in Brazil and in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, it was already common to attribute the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">gentile</a> to a person, usually of clear Portuguese descent, resident or whose family resided in the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Brazil" title="State of Brazil">State of Brazil</a> (1530-1815), belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>. During the lifetime of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a> (1815-1822), however, there was confusion about the nomenclature.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_nationality_law" title="Brazilian nationality law">Brazilian nationality law</a></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Constitution of Brazil</a>, a Brazilian citizen is:
</p>
<ul><li>Anyone born in Brazil, even if to foreign born parents. However, if the foreign parents were at the service of a foreign State (such as foreign <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomats</a>), the child is not Brazilian;</li>
<li>Anyone born abroad to a Brazilian father or a Brazilian mother, with registration of birth in a Brazilian Embassy or Consulate. Also, a person born abroad to a Brazilian father or a Brazilian mother who was not registered but who, after turning 18 years old, went to live in Brazil;<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>A foreigner living in Brazil who applied for and was accepted as a Brazilian citizen.</li></ul>
<p>According to the Constitution, all people who hold Brazilian citizenship are equal, regardless of race, ethnicity, gender or religion.
</p><p>A foreigner can apply for Brazilian citizenship after living for four uninterrupted years in Brazil and being able to speak Portuguese. A native person from an official Portuguese language country (<a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">São Tomé and Príncipe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea_Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinea Bissau">Guinea Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>) can request the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_nationality_law" title="Brazilian nationality law">Brazilian nationality</a> after only 1 uninterrupted year living in Brazil. A foreign born person who holds Brazilian citizenship has exactly the same <a href="/wiki/Rights" title="Rights">rights</a> and duties of the Brazilian citizen by birth, but cannot occupy some special public positions such as the Presidency of the Republic, Vice-presidency of the Republic, Minister (Secretary) of Defense, Presidency (Speaker) of the Senate, Presidency (Speaker) of the House of Representatives, Officer of the Armed Forces and Diplomat.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_Brazil" title="Race and ethnicity in Brazil">Race and ethnicity in Brazil</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous peoples of Brazil">Indigenous peoples of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Colonial Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian_history" title="Afro-Brazilian history">Afro-Brazilian history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">Immigration to Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Brazil" title="History of the Jews in Brazil">History of the Jews in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazilians are mostly <a href="/wiki/Kinship" title="Kinship">descendants</a> of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilians" title="Portuguese Brazilians">Portuguese settlers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">post-colonial</a> immigrant groups, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">Enslaved Africans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Brazil's indigenous peoples</a>. Along with other immigrants of who arrived in Brazil, from the 1820s well into the 1970s, most of the settlers were <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Brazilian">Italians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_immigration_to_Brazil" title="Spanish immigration to Brazil">Spaniards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilians" title="Arab Brazilians">Arabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/German-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="German-Brazilian">Germans</a>, with significantly large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Brazilians" title="Armenian Brazilians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Brazil" title="Romani people in Brazil">Gypsies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Brazilians" title="Greek Brazilians">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Brazilian">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian Brazilian">Ukrainians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilians" title="Arab Brazilians">Levantine Arabs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-j1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j1-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:334px;max-width:334px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:332px;max-width:332px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazilians_001.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Brazilians_001.JPG/330px-Brazilians_001.JPG" decoding="async" width="330" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Brazilians_001.JPG/495px-Brazilians_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Brazilians_001.JPG/660px-Brazilians_001.JPG 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="355" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The Brazilian people are multi-ethnic. First row: <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Brazilian">White</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="German Brazilian">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilians" title="Arab Brazilians">Arab</a>, respectively) and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese</a> Brazilians. Second row: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">African</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">pardo</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Cafuzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cafuzo">cafuzo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulato</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Caboclo" title="Caboclo">caboclo</a></i>, respectively) and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Native</a> (Indian) Brazilians.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:332px;max-width:332px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG/330px-Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG" decoding="async" width="330" height="197" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG/495px-Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG/660px-Main_ethnic_groups_in_brazil.JPG 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="424" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Main Brazilian ethnic groups</div></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span id="The_colonization_period_.281500_to_1822.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_colonization_period_(1500_to_1822)">The colonization period (1500 to 1822)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The colonization period (1500 to 1822)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The three principal groups were Native Brazilians, European colonizers and African labor.
</p>
<ul><li>Brazil was inhabited by an estimated 2.4 million <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Amerindians</a> before the first settlers arrived in the 16th century. They had been living there since the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> and still exist in many different tribes and ethnicities, amounting to the hundreds, giving them varying features, shapes and shades. There are different estimates for the Indigenous population around 1498, when the cohort commanded by <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Pacheco_Pereira" title="Duarte Pacheco Pereira">Duarte Pacheco Pereira</a> first set foot in Brazilian territory, followed by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> in 1500 and 1502, with figures revolving between 2.4 million and 3.1 million. What is more accurate is that about three quarters of them died from contracted diseases brought by colonizers (the <a href="/wiki/Flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Flu">flu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_fever" title="Scarlet fever">scarlet fever</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>) and conflicts (besides the numerous deaths in different tribal groups by forging alliances with the Portuguese, French and Dutch to fight each other, ending in genocide, the abortion rate also increased among Indigenous women after the arrival of the colonizers), while the remaining were pushed to the Amazon Basin, sometimes migrating beyond the borders with Hispanic provinces. It is also important to mention that a strong assimilation by miscegenation with local populations occurred, where Natives living under Jesuit protection and having a monastic life decided to leave for the life in towns. The European diseases spread quickly along the indigenous trade routes, and whole tribes were likely annihilated without ever coming in direct contact with Europeans. Today, 517,000 Indigenous people live in reservations and 160 thousand speak assorted Native languages, whereas millions of Brazilians have at least some degree of Amerindian ancestry due to the mentioned interracial encounters.</li>
<li>The country was officially discovered by Portugal in 1500 and received about 724,000 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> colonizers, mostly males, who settled there until the end of Colonial Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> But other sources even claim that the given numbers of total entrances were clearly surpassed. The Jesuits asked the Portuguese Crown to ship <a href="/wiki/Orphaned" class="mw-redirect" title="Orphaned">orphaned</a> women under royal wardship for marriage with the settlers; they were known as <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%93rf%C3%A3s_d%27El-Rei" title="Órfãs d&#39;El-Rei">Órfãs d'El-Rei</a></i> (modern <i>órfãs do rei</i>, "orphans of the king").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETelfer1932184_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETelfer1932184-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethell198447_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethell198447-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ensinarhistoria_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ensinarhistoria-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Daughters of noblemen who died overseas administrating captaincies in the colonies or in battle for the king would marry settlers of higher rank. Bahia's port in the Northeast received one of the first groups of orphans in 1551.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBethell198447_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBethell198447-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Portugal remained the only significant, but not an exclusive source of European immigration to Brazil until the early 19th century.
</p>
<ul><li>These other people came from different nationalities - but the by far most mentioned are the Dutch. Hence, under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a> in the northeastern part of the country, from 1630 to 1654, a comparatively small but still notable number of Dutch settlers (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Brazilian">Dutch Brazilian</a>) and some <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish People</a> arrived, the latter seeking religious freedom. These Jews founded the first Synagogue in the Americas, named <a href="/wiki/Kahal_Zur_Israel_Synagogue" title="Kahal Zur Israel Synagogue">Kahal Zur Israel Synagogue</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>.</li></ul>
<p>It is estimated that more than 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> entered <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, however, both groups had been forced out of the country after the rule's end. The remaining families mostly fled to remote parts of the interior of Northeastern Brazil (mainly in the states of Pernambuco, but also Paraíba, Rio Grande do Norte, Ceará and others) or changed their names to Portuguese ones. The proven excess of Y-chromosomes of the haplogroup 2 in northeasterners probably results from the high miscegenation of Dutch settlers with the local population.
</p><p>The Jews who mostly left Brazil took off to what was then named <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a>, today New York City, and founded the oldest Jewish congregation in the US, the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_Shearith_Israel" title="Congregation Shearith Israel">Congregation Shearith Israel</a>. The ones who stayed, converted into Christianity and were then known as <a href="/wiki/New_Christian" title="New Christian">New Christians</a> or <a href="/wiki/Marranos" class="mw-redirect" title="Marranos">Marranos</a>, who sometimes practiced <a href="/wiki/Crypto-Judaism" title="Crypto-Judaism">Crypto-Judaism</a>. Even if the Jewish population under Dutch Brazil not surpassed a few thousand individuals, a considerably higher number of New Christians, in the past simply absorbed as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese People">Portuguese</a> colonizers, arrived in Colonial Brazil - especially in the first centuries after 1500. They entered Brazil fleeing from the Inquisition or were deported by the Kingdom of Portugal and also Spain, latter being known as <a href="/wiki/Degredado" title="Degredado">Degredados</a>, someone who was sentenced or forced to exile. This also included <a href="/wiki/Romani_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani People">Romani People</a> from the Iberian Peninsula, what partially explains the curiously high numbers for a western country. Brazil has the second largest Gypsy population in the Americas after the US, having also received Roma people from Central and Eastern Europe, as well as the Baltic countries during the 20th century.
</p>
<ul><li>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> from the mid-16th century until 1855, an estimated 3.6 million <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="List of ethnic groups of Africa">African people</a>, also from many different countries and ethnicities were brought to Brazil, giving the country the Americas' largest population with some African ancestry. Many of the slaves suffered under severe conditions and the mortality rates were pretty high, what led to the foundation of <a href="/wiki/Quilombola" title="Quilombola">Quilombola</a> communities throughout the country. A small number of the slaves in the state of Bahia were actually Muslims; they produced a revolt in the city of Salvador that was quickly tamed by the army.</li></ul>
<p>In 1808, the <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">Portuguese court moved to Brazil</a>, bringing thousands of Portuguese again and afterwards opened its seaports to other nations starting from 1820. This caused the biggest wave of immigration which the country has seen until then.
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Great_Immigration_.281820_until_the_1970s.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Great_Immigration_(1820_until_the_1970s)">The Great Immigration (1820 until the 1970s)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Great Immigration (1820 until the 1970s)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg/220px-Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg/330px-Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg/440px-Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="496" data-file-height="357" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europeans_and_Arabs_in_Brazil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some of the main immigrant groups</div></div></div>
<p>In this period, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">people</a> from all over the world officially entered Brazil, the vast majority of them Europeans.
</p><p>Between 1820 and the 1950s, Brazil received around <b>5,686,133</b> European immigrants, including a thriving Jewish population.<sup id="cite_ref-Brazil_-_Modern-Day_Community_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brazil_-_Modern-Day_Community-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In addition, 950,000 Asians settled in Brazil throughout the 20th century, including considerable numbers of Middle Easterners or Christian Levantine Arabs and 270,000 Japanese, the highest figure among East Asians.<sup id="cite_ref-BailyMíguez2003_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BailyMíguez2003-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abril_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abril-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Entrada_de_estrangeiros_no_Brasil_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entrada_de_estrangeiros_no_Brasil-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Back then, nearly <b>70&#160;%</b> of those immigrants originated from <b>Southern Europe</b>.</li></ul>
<ul><li>A second wave of <b><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese</a></b> people arrived (here: <a href="/wiki/Postcolonialism" title="Postcolonialism">Postcolonialism</a>), this time with more than <b>1,8 million</b> immigrants.</li></ul>
<p>Portuguese people have been present since the discovery of the country, and therefore it is difficult to estimate a more accurate number of descendants. Millions of White Brazilians descend from recent Portuguese immigration from between the 1870s and 1975. In addition, many multiracial Brazilians partially descend from Portuguese people, caused by the high intermarriage rates. Most of them came from the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Portugal" title="Provinces of Portugal">historical provinces</a> of Minho, Trás-os-Montes, Beira, Estremadura (North and Central Portugal). Northeastern Brazil traditionally received the first waves of immigrants, but during the Great Immigration, the Southeast received the biggest influx. São Paulo (state) received the most, followed by Rio de Janeiro (city), which is considered the largest Portuguese city outside of Lisbon. The second former capital of Brazil once also was the capital of Portugal, the only European capital outside of Europe. The accent in the city of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> subsequently reminds the 19th century innovations that took place in the European variety of the language, while the prosody of the rest of the country, besides some local varieties, has rather conservative phonetics rooted in the 1600s. Other states with significant numbers were <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A1" title="Pará">Pará</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">Pernambuco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>. Nowadays, they naturally live throughout Brazil and compose the majority of White and also Multiracial Brazilians in many states.
</p>
<ul><li>Furthermore, around <b>1,6 million</b> <b><a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Brazilian">Italians</a></b> were responsible for a massive immigration wave, consequently composing the biggest European follow-up group the country has received after its colonizers.</li></ul>
<p>Today, millions of <a href="/wiki/Italian-Brazilians" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian-Brazilians">Italian-Brazilians</a> make Brazil their home, as they usually brought the whole family and had high birth rates. Regarding the total numbers, this probably represents the biggest Italian diaspora outside of Italy. Contrary to other countries, more than half of the Italians immigrated from the North, mostly composed by people from <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>, followed by people from Central Italy. The state of São Paulo had the strongest and a more diverse influx, with many also coming from <a href="/wiki/South_Italy" title="South Italy">South Italy</a>, especially to the eponymic capital. <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a> mostly went to <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo (state)</a>, which received half of the overall immigrants. The others mainly went to the states of southern Brazil, where they also composed the biggest European immigrant group. Other notable influxes occurred in two other southeastern states, here <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Espírito Santo">Espírito Santo</a> and the Central-West region, mainly to <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso_do_Sul" title="Mato Grosso do Sul">Mato Grosso do Sul</a> and Goiás. Comparatively small numbers went to <a href="/wiki/Pernambuco" title="Pernambuco">Pernambuco</a> and Bahia, both in the Northeast. Nowadays the descendants mostly live in mentioned areas, but the sheer amount and internal migrations made the Italilan diaspora spread out and nowadays they are scattered all over Brazil.
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Brazilians_of_Spanish_descent" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilians of Spanish descent">Spaniards</a></b> also arrived in rather high numbers, with around <b>700,000</b> immigrants mainly from <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Several million Brazilians have Spanish ancestry. Most Spaniards settled in the past century, where they chiefly headed to <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>. Most notably from <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> (South), others from the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> (North and East Spain) followed. Galicians were also present throughout Colonial Brazil, as the province shares borders and linguistic ties with Portugal, and once was part of the country. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Brazilian">Spanish Brazilians</a> in the other states mainly have origins in <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, which arrived in earlier occasions. Many of them went to the first capital <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a> and its state Bahia, but also Pernambuco (Northeast), Pará (North), <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Espírito Santo">Espírito Santo</a> (Southeast), and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a> (South).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Note:</b> Brazil is also home to other Southern European populations, mainly <a href="/wiki/Greek_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Brazilian">Greeks</a> (around 150,000 descendants), but they are by far the smallest groups with origins in South Europe.
</p><p>2) The remaining <b>30&#160;%</b> were composed of <b>Other Europeans</b>, <b>Asians</b> (Western and Eastern Asia), <b>Africans</b> (many White Africans, Jews, Berbers and others) and <b>Americans</b> (South and North Americans).
</p>
<ul><li><b>Other Europeans:</b></li></ul>
<p>- Western Europeans were very present, as around <b>240,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/German_Brazilians" title="German Brazilians">Germans</a></b> settled, <b>198,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/Austrian_Brazilians" title="Austrian Brazilians">Austrian</a></b> and <b>52,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/Swiss_Brazilians" title="Swiss Brazilians">Swiss</a></b>; <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg Brazilian">Luxembourgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volga_Germans" title="Volga Germans">Volga Germans</a> were also documented, but in comparatively low numbers. <b>German speaking nationalities</b> were the fourth largest European immigration group and today German is the second most spoken mother tongue in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In addition, <b>150,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/French_Brazilians" title="French Brazilians">French</a></b> immigrants entered Brazilian ports, where <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Brazilians" title="Belgian Brazilians">Belgian</a> and <b><a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazilians" title="Dutch Brazilians">Dutch</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-swierenga.com_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swierenga.com-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paraná_State_Government_page_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paraná_State_Government_page-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> (not to be confused with Dutch Brazil) settlers also were listed.
</p><p>- Eastern Europeans were relatively numerous, with more than <b>350,000</b> listed immigrants. This included <b>154,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/Polish_Brazilians" title="Polish Brazilians">Poles</a></b>, around <b>40,000</b> <b><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Brazilians" title="Ukrainian Brazilians">Ukrainians</a></b> and smaller numbers of <b><a href="/wiki/Russian_Brazilians" title="Russian Brazilians">Russians</a></b>. These immigrants were searching for better opportunities - a few thousand <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> were also among them.<sup id="cite_ref-br.sputniknews.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br.sputniknews.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MSZ_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSZ-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vanhoni.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanhoni.com-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rcub.com.br_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rcub.com.br-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> from other regions migrated as well, here mainly <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a> like Bulgarians and Croats, but also Czechs and Slovaks, with moderate numbers of Slovenes and others.<sup id="cite_ref-revistas.usp.br_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistas.usp.br-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Câmara_de_Comércio_Brasil-Rússia_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Câmara_de_Comércio_Brasil-Rússia-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <b><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Brazilians" title="Hungarian Brazilians">Hungarians</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-mfa.gov.hu_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa.gov.hu-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> were among the non-Slavic Eastern Europeans and were the biggest groups after the Poles, Russians and Ukrainians.
</p><p>- Northern Europeans were the least numerous, but also present. More than <b>78,000</b> <a href="/wiki/English_Brazilians" title="English Brazilians">Britons</a>, mainly under <b><a href="/wiki/English_Brazilians" title="English Brazilians">English</a></b> passports, and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Brazilians" title="Scottish Brazilians">Scots</a> entered the country. They dispersed to different regions: a few <a href="/wiki/Irish_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Brazilian">Irish</a> people went to already urbanized regions.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ingleses_no_Brasil_do_século_XIX_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingleses_no_Brasil_do_século_XIX-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fluminense_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fluminense-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <b><a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Brazilians" title="Scandinavian Brazilians">Scandinavian people</a></b>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Brazilians" title="Scandinavian Brazilians">Swedes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Brazilians" title="Scandinavian Brazilians">Norwegians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-scandinavian-association_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scandinavian-association-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> were both listed and sent over <b>40,000</b> immigrants each, as well as around <b>17,000</b> Danes. <b>3,400</b> <a href="/wiki/Estonians" title="Estonians">Estonians</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and a rather small number of <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Brazilians" title="Finnish Brazilians">Finns</a> were also present. Even smaller and therefore often forgotten, an influx from <a href="/wiki/Icelanders" title="Icelanders">Icelanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faroese_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Faroese people">Faroese</a> was recorded, but they still left few thousand descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The Baltic region was also entirely present, where <b><a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_Brazilians" title="Lithuanian Brazilians">Lithuanians</a></b> composed the most numerous group, with over <b>50,000</b> entrances, followed by a much smaller number of Latvians.<sup id="cite_ref-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Um_atalho_para_a_Europa-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lithuanian_descendants_in_Brazil_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lithuanian_descendants_in_Brazil-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ilas.columbia.edu_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilas.columbia.edu-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>- European Jews of Ashkenazi origin, more precisely around <b>48,000</b> people from several countries, chose Brazil as their destination. <b><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Brazil" title="History of the Jews in Brazil">Ashkenazi Jews</a></b> were first documented during Imperial times, when the liberal second emperor of Brazil welcomed a few thousands of families facing persecution in Europe during the 1870s and 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary.org_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary.org-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Two heavier influxes took place during the 20th century. The earliest right after the Great War and the second inrush between the 1930s and 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-MSZ_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSZ-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary.org_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary.org-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
Brazil has also seen an influx from North African Jews of Sephardic origin coming from mainly Morocco and Egypt, which were counted extra.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Asians</b>:</li></ul>
<p>- Western Asians, more specifically from the <b><a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a></b> region, equally arrived in large numbers, chiefly <b><a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Brazilians" title="Lebanese Brazilians">Lebanese</a></b> and <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Brazilians" title="Syrian Brazilians">Syrians</a>, both surpassing <b>200,000</b> entrances throughout the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> with mentionable numbers of <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Brazilian">Armenian</a>, Georgian and some <a href="/wiki/Iranian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian people">Iranian</a> immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region.
</p><p>- East Asians, the majority composed of <b><a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">Japanese</a></b> immigrants, also arrived in formidable numbers, where the first ship landed in 1908, surpassing <b>250,000</b> immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-Abril_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abril-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-japantimes_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japantimes-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-japao100.com.br_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japao100.com.br-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IBGE_traça_perfil_dos_imigrantes_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBGE_traça_perfil_dos_imigrantes-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> But <b><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Brazilians" title="Chinese Brazilians">Chinese</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Korean_Brazilians" title="Korean Brazilians">Koreans</a></b> also have traditions of immigrating to Brazil, especially after the 1950s, with around 200,000 and 100,000 immigrants respectively.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Americans:</b></li></ul>
<p>- North Americans also formed the melting pot that is Brazil, with the country being one of the few which received <a href="/wiki/Americans_in_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Americans in Brazil">US-Americans</a> who fled the American Civil War, settling in Southeastern and Southern Brazil during the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Reconstruction Era">American reconstruction period</a>. In addition, smaller numbers of North Americans immigrated after 1808.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Lost_Colony_of_the_Confederacy_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Lost_Colony_of_the_Confederacy-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TSHA_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TSHA-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The descendants of those <b><a href="/wiki/Confederate_colonies" title="Confederate colonies">Confederate colonies</a></b> are culturally known as the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Confederados" title="Confederados">Confederados</a></b></i> sub-group, especially in the countryside of São Paulo, where they founded towns and their presence was stronger<sup id="cite_ref-The_Lost_Colony_of_the_Confederacy_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Lost_Colony_of_the_Confederacy-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> - Brazilians of US-American descent can be found throughout the country, resulting from other periods and the dispersion of the Confederados descendants, who are nowadays mostly mixed with other groups and sometimes mistaken for descendants of British immigrants. Ethnically the Confederados were mostly English-Welsh, Scottish, Irish, German and Scandinavian.<sup id="cite_ref-Eugene_C._Harter_1985,_p._74_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eugene_C._Harter_1985,_p._74-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>- South Americans were strongly represented by Argentines since the 18th century and always had a strong community in the country. They still form one of the largest South American immigrant groups in Brazil, nowadays only surpassed by Bolivians (see modern times). Uruguayan citizens after the country's independence from the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> were also noticeable throughout the 19th and 20th centuries.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Africans:</b></li></ul>
<p>- North African regions, historically distinguished from <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, also sent immigrants. This time they mainly came from Egypt, with around <b>10,000</b> people, than the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region, especially Morocco (mostly Jews who went to Northern Brazil). Therefore, a stronger influx from other cultures occurred, contrary to Colonial Brazil, where most Africans were forced labor work brought from the Black populations.
</p><p>- Other Africa-born people mainly include Dutch South-Africans (<a href="/wiki/Afrikaner" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaner">Boeren or Afrikaners</a>) and people from the former Portuguese Empire, mainly Angola (during the Great Immigration, but especially after the Civil Wars post-independence). Here people of several ethnicities immigrated (mainly Africans of European descent, but also Blacks and Coloured people).
</p><p><b>Note:</b> Dozen other immigrant groups form sizable communities with some varying number of descendants (5,000 to + 30 million). <b>Only in this period</b>, the port of <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos, São Paulo</a>, which was widely known as the most important entrance of immigrants in Brazil, received people from <b>more than 60 different countries</b>. Other important ports, which occasionally received other immigrant groups as the before mentioned, were the ones in the cities of Rio de Janeiro, Porto Alegre, Vitória, Recife etc.<sup id="cite_ref-j1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j1-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Modern_times_.281970_to_now.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times_(1970_to_now)">Modern times (1970 to now)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern times (1970 to now)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Not to be compared with the great immigration before, a still ongoing influx from Africa (Angola, Senegal) and South America and the Caribbean (Bolivia, Paraguay, Chile, Uruguay, Haiti, Suriname, Jamaica, Barbados) is happening since the late 1960's. Asian immigrants (from Palestine, China, South Korea, returning Japanese Brazilians, <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Dutch Indonesians</a>, Afghans and immigrants from Vietnam, Iran, Pakistan, the Philippines and others) as well as European immigrants (Portugal due to ties, young qualified professionals from Western Europe, especially after 2008, Northern Europeans who seek warmer weather and several Eastern Europeans) are thriving in varying numbers.
</p><p>After 1975 large groups of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Surinamese" title="Dutch Surinamese">Dutch Surinamese or Boeroes</a> immigrated to Brazil due to the independence in Suriname. Most of them settled in the countryside of São Paulo and Paraná where there are thriving <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazilians" title="Dutch Brazilians">Dutch Brazilian</a> colonies.
</p><p><b>Current foreign population</b>
</p><p>In 2011, the country was home to 1.5 million <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign born</a> people, more than twice as of 2009.
</p><p>The numbers still could be higher, as there are many undocumented people in Brazil as well. For both, the documented and undocumented, most of the foreigners come from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, China, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, Spain, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, Japan and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The major work visas concessions were granted for citizens of the United States and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lusitanian immigration never ceased throughout the 19th and 20th centuries. Portuguese people in diaspora settled in Brazil especially during the 1970s coming from former Portuguese colonies like <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> or Angola after its independence. 
An additional figure of <b>1.2 million Portuguese</b> arrived between 1951 and 1975 to settle mostly in the Southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> 
Nowadays, Lusitanians constitute the biggest group of foreigners living in the country, with over 690,000 Portuguese nationals currently living in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority arrived in the last decade. The first semester of 2011 solely had an increase of 52 thousand Portuguese nationals applying for a permanent residence visa while another large group was granted Brazilian citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, people of more than 220 nationalities have communities in Brazil, 40 of them more than 10,000 people.
</p><p><b>Refugees</b>
</p><p>In 2014, Brazil was home to 5,208 <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> from 79 different <a href="/wiki/Nationalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalities">nationalities</a>. The three largest refugee ancestries were <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syrian</a> (1,626), <a href="/wiki/Colombian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian people">Colombian</a> (1,154) and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angolan</a> (1062). In addition to these numbers, there are several thousand people who had entered the country and are still waiting for the government to acknowledge their refugee status, as 1,830 people from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a><sup id="cite_ref-Mundo_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mundo-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> in 2013 alone and other 1,021 people from Syria and 799 people from <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, for example.<sup id="cite_ref-Mundo_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mundo-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Brazil is today home to 4.5 thousand Afghans and was a destination for <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_boat_people" title="Vietnamese boat people">Vietnamese boat people</a> in the past.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispersal_of_races_and_colours_in_the_country">Dispersal of races and colours in the country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Dispersal of races and colours in the country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Note:</b> The ethnic composition of Brazilians is not uniform across the country.
</p>
<ul><li>Due to its large influx of <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> immigrants in the 19th and 20th centuries, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Brazil">Southern Region</a> have a <b>White</b> majority (mostly Europeans of Italian, Portuguese, German, Austrian, Swiss, Slavic, Dutch and Spanish ancestry).<sup id="cite_ref-sidra.ibge.gov.br_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sidra.ibge.gov.br-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">Rio de Janeiro</a> has a sizable white population slightly over 50% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The other two Southeastern states, Minas Gerais and Espírito Santo,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> are around 50% White (the Southeast region also includes Levantine Arabs).<sup id="cite_ref-sidra.ibge.gov.br_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sidra.ibge.gov.br-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> São Paulo has the largest absolute number with 30 million Whites, followed by Minas Gerais, Rio Grande do Sul, Rio de Janeiro and Paraná, while Santa Catarina, where 86% of the population has European phenotype, reaches the highest percentage.<sup id="cite_ref-sidra.ibge.gov.br_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sidra.ibge.gov.br-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The cities of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_city" class="mw-redirect" title="São Paulo city">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro city">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a> have the largest populations of <b><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Brazil" title="History of the Jews in Brazil">Ashkenazi Jews</a></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brazil_-_Modern-Day_Community_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brazil_-_Modern-Day_Community-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most <b>East Asians</b>, especially <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">Japanese Brazilians</a>, the largest group, live in São Paulo and Paraná.<sup id="cite_ref-japao100.com.br_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japao100.com.br-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Most Koreans also live in São Paulo whereas the Chinese diaspora is spread particularly throughout the Southeast. Rio de Janeiro has a large Chinese population following São Paulo.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeastern Brazil">Northeastern Region</a>, the first occupied and therefore most mixed region, has larger numbers of people with darker features, with stronger African, Romani, Amerindian and Sephardi influences from Colonial Brazil. The <b>majority</b> there is composed of <b>Pardo (mixed) people</b>, who are of a brownish or darker phenotype with light to dark features, followed by Whites (mostly Europeans and also with admixtures) and then by people with mostly African blood - Bahia and Maranhão have the biggest Black African populations in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The individual appearance of Pardo people varies extremely, but generally all types and colours of hairs, eyes and skin are involved (usually not the extremes as extremely white or extremely black). But in fact, minorities in the White and Black populations consider themselves as Pardo. Moreover, some people in the Roma, Sephardic, Arab and Asian population classify themselves as Pardo, due to miscegenation with other races.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Brazil">Northern Brazil</a>, largely covered by the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a>, is also mostly <b>Pardo</b>, due to a stronger <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> influence.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The two remaining <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Brazil">South Eastern states</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Central-West Region, Brazil">Central-Western</a> Brazil have a more <b>balanced</b> ratio among different racial groups (around 50% White, 43% Pardo, 5% Black, 1% Asian/Amerindian).</li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics</a> (IBGE) classifies the Brazilian population in five categories: <i>brancos</i> (<a href="/wiki/Whites" class="mw-redirect" title="Whites">white</a>), <i>negros</i> (<a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">pardos</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Brown_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Brown people">brown or mixed</a>), <i>amarelos</i> (<a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian/yellow</a>) and <i>índios</i> (<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Amerindian</a>), based on <a href="/wiki/Human_skin_color" title="Human skin color">skin color</a> or <a href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (classification of human beings)">race</a>. The last detailed census (PNAD) found Brazil to be made up of c. 91 million white people (<a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Brazilian">White Brazilian</a>), 79 million multiracial people (<a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a>), 14 million black people (<a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">Afro-Brazilian</a>), 2-4 million Asian people (<a href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian Brazilian</a>) and 807,900 indigenous (<a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a>) people.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg/220px-Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg/330px-Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg/440px-Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Concentra%C3%A7%C3%A3o.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young Brazilians</div></div></div>
<p>In the 2005 detailed census, for the first time in two decades, the number of White Brazilians did not exceed 50% of the population. On the other side, the number of <i>pardos</i> (multiracial) people increased and all the others remained almost the same. According to the IBGE, this trend is mainly because of the revaluation of the identity of historically discriminated ethnic groups.
</p><p>Brazil is said to be among the most miscegenated countries in the world, as since the country was discovered and during the colonial period intermarriage between races was never illegal and common. Those of full ancestry are usually the Brazilians who can trace back their ethnicity to more recent immigration from the monarchical period in the 19th century until the Republican 20th and 21st centuries. Still, many Brazilians can not trace back their real origin easily. For instance, European family names which were difficult to pronounce were commonly changed to easier Portuguese surnames. In basic terms, it could be said that half of Brazilians are descendants of populations from the colonial era and the other half made of modern immigration. Brazil is a true melting pot of Europeans, Asians, Africans and Indigenous people, who either are in the single group or a mixture of various different backgrounds and races.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="White_coloured_people">White coloured people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: White coloured people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Brazilian">White Brazilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">Immigration to Brazil</a></div>
<p><b>Whites</b> constitute the majority of Brazil's population regarding the total numbers within a single racial group, having the most numerous population in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>.
</p><p>The country has the second largest <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Brazilian">White population</a> in the Americas, with around 91,051,646 people.
</p><p>And White Brazilians make up the <b>third</b> largest <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White population</a> in the world, after the United States and Russia, also counting in total numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-ibge.gov.br_2010_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibge.gov.br_2010-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority came from the Great Immigration period, which was the large European influx after steps had been taken for "whitening policies" during the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Monarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Brazilian_Republic" title="First Brazilian Republic">Early Republican</a> periods. Those policies also sought labor and also were made in order to avoid the foreign invasion threat of sparsely populated areas in the South. Various other groups derive from <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">colonial times</a> and post-war decades.
</p><p>There are people of European descent distributed throughout the entire territory of Brazil, however, Southeast and South Brazil have the largest White populations. Whereas the Southeast region has the largest absolute numbers, <b>79.8%</b> of the population in the three southernmost states has European or Caucasian phenotype.
The state of <b><a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a></b> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Brazil">Southern Brazil</a> has the highest percentage, being almost <b>90% European</b>. <b><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a></b> in the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Brazil">Southeast</a> has the fourth highest rate, but is the state with the most Whites in <b>absolute numbers of 30 million <a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">Whites</a></b>, mainly from Europe, also having largest Levantine Arab and Jewish populations.
</p>

<p>Brazil is home to <b>240</b> immigrant or extoctone languages, most of them European languages. <b><a href="/wiki/Geographical_distribution_of_German_speakers" title="Geographical distribution of German speakers">Standard German and German dialects</a></b> make the <b>second most spoken</b> language in Brazil with around <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_German" title="Brazilian German">4 million bilingual speakers</a> or 2% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-olivet.edu_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olivet.edu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-revistas.usp.br_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistas.usp.br-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ligma_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ligma-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_hunsrik_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue_hunsrik-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> other Caucasoid immigration languages are <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a></b> or <b><a href="/wiki/Talian_dialect" title="Talian dialect">Talian dialect</a></b>,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue.com_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue.com-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-periodicos.ufes.br_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-periodicos.ufes.br-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-seer.ufu.br_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seer.ufu.br-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-revistas.usp.br_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistas.usp.br-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Castilian, Ukrainian,<sup id="cite_ref-revistas.usp.br_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistas.usp.br-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Russian,<sup id="cite_ref-br.sputniknews.com_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br.sputniknews.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Dutch,<sup id="cite_ref-revistas.usp.br_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistas.usp.br-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ligma_4-10" class="reference"><a </p><p>Assorted German dialects (including the ancient <b><a href="/wiki/East_Pomeranian_dialect" title="East Pomeranian dialect">East Pomeranian dialect</a></b>, practically extinct in Europe)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and Venetian or Talian share <b>co-official status</b> with Portuguese in several municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-rslei_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rslei-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsleijulho2012_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsleijulho2012-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span id="Mixed_.28multiracial.29_people"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mixed_(multiracial)_people">Mixed (multiracial) people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mixed (multiracial) people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pardo_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Pardo Brazilian">Pardo Brazilian</a></div>
<p><b>Multiracials</b> constitute the second largest group of Brazil, with around 84,7 million people. The term <i>Pardo</i> or mixed race Brazilian is a rather complex one. Multiracial Brazilians appear in hundreds of different shades, colours and backgrounds. They are typically a mixture of colonial and post-colonial <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a> with descendants of <a href="/wiki/African_slaves" class="mw-redirect" title="African slaves">African slaves</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous peoples of the Americas</a>. Some individuals may also descend from Maghreb people, Jews, Middle Eastern and Egyptian people, or a more recent ancestry from East or South Asia. Skin colours can vary from light to dark. The <i><b>caboclo</b></i> or <i><b>mestiço</b></i> population, those who are a miscegenation of Native and European, revolves around 43 million people. Genetic studies conducted by the geneticist Sergio D.J. Pena of the Federal University of Minas Gerais have shown that the <b><a href="/wiki/Caboclo" title="Caboclo">Caboclo</a></b> population is made of individuals whose DNA ranges from 70% to 90% European (mostly Portuguese, Spanish, Dutch, French or Italian 1500s to 1700s male settlers) with the remaining percentage spanning different Indigenous markers. Similar DNA tests showed that people self-classified as <b><a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulatto</a></b> or White and Black mix, span from 62% to 85% European (mostly descendants of Portuguese, Dutch and French settlers during the colonial period in the Northeast). The <b>Pardo category</b> in Brazil also includes 800 thousand <b><a href="/wiki/Gypsies" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsies">Gypsies</a></b> or <b><a href="/wiki/Roma_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma people">Roma people</a></b>, most of them coming from Portugal but also different countries in Eastern Europe and the Baltics. <b><a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasians</a></b> can also be classified as Pardo. The majority of them consisting of <b><a href="/wiki/Hafu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hafu">Ainoko</a></b> or <b><a href="/wiki/Hafu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hafu">Hafu</a></b>, individuals who are a miscegenation between Japanese and European.
</p><p>Recent research has suggested that Asians from the early <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Eastern_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Eastern Empire">Portuguese Eastern Empire</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Luso-Asians" title="Luso-Asians">Luso-Asians</a> first came to Brazil during the sixteenth century as seamen known as <a href="/wiki/Lascars" class="mw-redirect" title="Lascars">Lascars</a>, or as servants, slaves and <a href="/wiki/Concubines" class="mw-redirect" title="Concubines">concubines</a> accompanying the governors, merchants and clergy who has served in Portuguese Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> This first presence of Asians was limited to <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast Brazil">Northeast Brazil</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>, but others were brought as cultivators, textile workers and miners to <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A1" title="Pará">Pará</a> and other parts of the Northeast.
</p><p>The largest populations with Pardo individuals are found in northern and northeastern Brazil, with many inhabiting the states of <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A1s" title="Goiás">Goiás</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Espírito Santo">Espírito Santo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">Rio de Janeiro (state)</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo (state)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná (state)</a>, as well as the Federal District. While the occurrence of Pardos is not uniform across the country, there are states with more people of mixed background than others. It also can happen that Pardos constitute significant numbers within single regions in states.
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_coloured_people">Black coloured people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Black coloured people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">Afro-Brazilian</a></div>
<p><b>Blacks</b> constitute the third largest ethnic group of Brazil with around 14,5 million citizens or 7,6&#160;% of the population. These are people who have origins in any of the black populations of Africa. In the country, these are generally used for Brazilians with at least partial <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan African">Sub-Saharan African</a> ancestry. Most African Brazilians are the direct descendants of captive Africans who survived the slavery era within the boundaries of the present Brazil, but also with considerable European and Amerindian ancestry. Afro-Brazilians might not directly be compared to Pardo-Brazilians. The number of African genes is substantially higher in Afro-Brazilians, therefore their skin colour is darker compared to mixed-race Brazilians.
Brazil, followed by the US, has the largest <b><a href="/wiki/African_diaspora" title="African diaspora">African diaspora</a></b> in the Americas.
</p><p>Today most Blacks are either Catholic or Evangelical. Smaller groups are Irreligious including Atheists and a number of African tradition sects can be found especially in Bahia, notably <a href="/wiki/Candombl%C3%A9" title="Candomblé">Candomblé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umbanda" title="Umbanda">Umbanda</a>. The latter being a syncretism of Roman Catholicism, African traditions, <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">Spiritism</a> and Indigenous beliefs. A minority of Blacks follows <a href="/wiki/Kardecism" class="mw-redirect" title="Kardecism">Kardecism</a>, which is a blend of Christianism and <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">Spiritualism</a> founded in France.
</p><p>Most Blacks can be found in Bahia and Maranhão states after the colonial period influx, as well as in the northern region of Minas Gerais thanks to the Diamond and Gold Rush period and parts of Rio de Janeiro due to slavery in the former royal court after its transfer.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asian_Brazilians">Asian Brazilians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Asian Brazilians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian Brazilian</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese Brazilian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Brazilian">Chinese Brazilian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Korean_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean Brazilian">Korean Brazilian</a></div>
<p><b>Asians</b>, in common parlance referred to East-Asians, constitute the fourth largest ethnic group of Brazil with <b>2.2 million</b> people, what may not include mixed East Asians. The largest East-Asian ethnic group in the country are the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese</a>. 
Brazil has the largest population of Japanese people outside Japan, being in percentage or absolute numbers. The number of Japanese Brazilians revolves around <b>1.8 million</b> descendants and the Japanese community also comprises <b>57 thousand Japanese nationals</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-japantimes_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japantimes-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-japao100.com.br_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japao100.com.br-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IBGE_traça_perfil_dos_imigrantes_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBGE_traça_perfil_dos_imigrantes-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> According to Ethnologue over <b>400 thousand people speak Japanese</b> in Brazil.
</p><p>The others are mainly Chinese, Taiwanese and South Korean. Due to the recent immigration of Chinese citizens to Brazil the number of these people is constantly on the rise.
</p><p>South Asians also left descendants in Brazil, mostly East Indians, Vietnamese, Indonesians and Bengali. However, there is a current stronger influx of Bengalis (between 5 and 10,000) nowadays, most of them refugees. Moreover, South Asians might not be included into the category of people with "yellow" skin colour, as they are physically different from Eastern Asian populations and therefore more likely to fit into the Pardo category.
</p><p>There are large groups of East Asian Catholics as well as non-religious Asians. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Brazil" title="Buddhism in Brazil">Buddhism in Brazil</a> is also very common among non-Asians, especially Whites, with Japanese Buddhism being among the most usual and oldest forms. <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">Shinto</a> practices involving life style and funerals are very common in Nipponese families of São Paulo and Paraná states. Shinto-derived <a href="/wiki/Japanese_New_Religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese New Religions">Japanese New Religions</a> are very popular throughout the nation. The largest Nipponese new religions are <a href="/wiki/Seicho-no-Ie" title="Seicho-no-Ie">Seicho-no-Ie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenrikyo" title="Tenrikyo">Tenrikyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/PL_Kyodan" title="PL Kyodan">Perfect Liberty Kyodan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Church_of_World_Messianity" title="Church of World Messianity">Church of World Messianity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Korean_Confucianism" title="Korean Confucianism">Korean Confucianism</a> and Chinese Confucianism are especially found in São Paulo capital.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_people">Indigenous people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Indigenous people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Native_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Brazilian">Native Brazilian</a></div>
<p><b>Indigenous people</b> constitute the fifth largest ethnic group of Brazil, with around <b>800,000</b> individuals. It is the oldest ethnic group in the country, mainly located in the surroundings of the Amazon basin inside the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Forest">Amazon Forest</a> but also in various reservations throughout the five geographical regions. Compared to the total population of the country the number might seem small, but millions of Brazilians actually have some Indigenous ancestry. This happened mainly because of the miscegenation of indigenous tribes with colonial settlers.
</p><p>Around <b>180 Native or autoctone languages are spoken in Brazil</b> by 160 thousand people, many of them have threatened status. Most Natives can communicate in Portuguese and tribes in reservations have their mother tongue and Portuguese taught at schools. Today 517 thousand people live in Indigenous reservations.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_studies">Genetic studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Genetic studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Genetic studies have shown the Brazilian population as a whole to have European, African and Native Americans components.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autosomal_studies">Autosomal studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Autosomal studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2015 autosomal genetic study, which also analysed data of 25 studies of 38 different Brazilian populations concluded that: European ancestry accounts for 62% of the heritage of the population, followed by the African (21%) and the Native American (17%). The European contribution is highest in Southern Brazil (77%), the African highest in Northeast Brazil (27%) and the Native American is the highest in Northern Brazil (32%).<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
